C) First principles are innate and need no sensory input.
D) The sense provides the middle term for demonstration.

Key Takeaway
Sense provides raw particulars; the intellect abstracts universals and recognizes self-evident truths as the foundation of all knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Three Additional Ways Sense Aids the Intellect: Induction, Experience, and Intuition
Three additional modes of sensory aid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between induction, experience, and intuition as modes of sensory assistance to the intellect, and identify which type of knowledge each yields.

Core Idea
Beyond abstraction, sense aids the intellect through induction, experience, and intuition, each with a distinct scope.

After explaining abstraction, the author briefly notes three other ways the senses assist the intellect: induction (istiqra'), experience (tajriba), and intuition (hads). Induction uses sense data and first principles to reach general conclusions; experience provides knowledge that only comes from repeated observation; and intuition grasps the cause of known matters. This lesson clarifies these distinctions and their epistemic roles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three additional ways
Locate the sentence beginning with 'wa qad yasta'inu al-'aql...' and list each method: al-istiqra', al-tajriba, al-hads.
The author says ta'mu 'bic' for experience, meaning repeated observation.
2
Contrast each method's domain
Induction relies on first principles and sense; experience works only in matters not obtainable otherwise; intuition grasps causes.
3
Connect to the overall epistemology
These methods show that sense is indispensable even for higher forms of knowledge, but the intellect remains the ultimate arbiter.

The Theoretical Intellect: The Source of First Principles
Theoretical intellect as source of first principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why first principles cannot be acquired by demonstration or knowledge, and why the theoretical intellect is their source.

Core Idea
First principles are not proven; they are the innate endowment of the theoretical intellect.

The author concludes the passage with a profound epistemological insight: the starting point of demonstration (burhan) cannot itself come from demonstration. Similarly, the starting point of knowledge cannot come from knowledge. There is only one power fit for this — the theoretical intellect ('aql nazari). This lesson explores this foundational principle of Islamic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key assertion
The author states that mabda' al-burhan (the starting point of demonstration) is not acquired by burhan, and mabda' al-'ilm (starting point of knowledge) is not acquired by the power of knowledge.
2
Identify the faculty responsible
The faculty that grasps first principles is al-'aql al-nazari (the theoretical intellect). It is the only power suitable for this.
3
Reflect on the implication
This means that foundational truths are not derived from reasoning or sense alone; they are immediate givens of the intellect, which then uses them in demonstration.

Specific Assent vs Absolute Assent: Refuting an Objection
Author refutes objection about assent types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between specific and absolute assent and explain why a common person's assent differs from a specialist's.

Core Idea
Assent is not one-size-fits-all: the specialist requires specific proof, the common person assents through inclination.

This lesson addresses a common misconception that any form of persuasion suffices for knowledge. The author rebuts an objection that absolute assent is enough, showing that the type of assent depends on the audience's cognitive capacity. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the right method of teaching and da'wah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find the hypothetical objector's claim: that absolute assent is sufficient for any learner, so any persuasion benefits absolute assent.
The objector confuses general assent with the specific assent required for knowledge.
2
Distinguish specific and absolute assent
Note that specific assent (tasdiq khas) is the type sought by specialists, while absolute assent (tasdiq mutlaq) is a weaker, general affirmation.
The author insists that the specialist's assent cannot be produced by mere inclination.
3
Analyze the common person's process
The common person assents when his soul inclines towards a proposition and he removes the opposite from his mind, even without rigorous proof.
Inclination is a cause of assent for the common person, not the assent itself.
4
Understand the role of inclination
The soul's inclination is concomitant with assent and acts as its cause, but it is not identical to the specific assent of the specialist.
This distinction justifies using different types of address for different audiences.
5
Connect to the broader purpose
The author uses this distinction to introduce the three types of address: demonstrative, rhetorical, and dialectical, each suited to a different audience.
The rebuttal sets up the Quranic proof for the three methods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس لقائل أن يقول إن التصديق أعم من التصديق الخاصي فيكون المتعلم إذا أقنع في المبادئ كيف كان فقد أفاد التصديق المطلق وإن لم يفد التصديق الخاصي. فإنَّا نقول إن الخاصي لو رفع له بمثل هذه الصفة تصديق من جنس التصديق العامي لكان يحق علينا أن نقول: إن هذه المخاطبة تفيده تصديقا وإن لم يكن تصديقًا خاصيًّا لكن الشاعر بالتصديق الخاصي ليس من شأنه أن ينفع له التصديق إلا على النحو الخاصي أو الشبيه به الذي لا يخطر ما يقابله بالبال . وأما العامي فلا يشعر بذلك بل يأخذ الأمر مصدقا به إذا مالت إليه نفسه، ويجري أن يمنط المقابل عن ذهنه وإن لاح له حواره فيكون ميل نفسه إليه مقارنا للتصديق، وعلة له وإن لم يكن نفس التصديق وإلا لا يكون هناك تصديق، ولا ظن مؤكد بل مثل ظن وميل النفس يوقع التصديق عند العامي؛ إذ نظره في ظاهر الشيء أي شيء كان. وبالجملة فكما أن المخاطبة البرهانية لا يبعد أن يراد بها العلية. وكذلك المخاطبة الخطابية فكذلك المخاطبة الجدلية لا يبعد أن يعدل باستعمالها عن جهتها إلى جهة التصديق. وقد نطق الكتاب الذي لا يأتيه الباطل من بين يديه ولا من خلفه فقال: ﴿ ادْعُ إِلَى سَبِيلِ رَبِّكَ بِالْحِكْمَةِ وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ وَجَادِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ ﴾ أي بالبرهان؛ وذلك ممن يحتمله وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ أي الخطابة؛ وذلك ممن يقتصر عنه، وَجَادِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ أي بالمشهورات المحمودة، فقدم البرهان والخطابة لما أنهما مصروفتان إلى الفائدة، والمجادلة مصروفة إلى المفاوضة ، والخطابة ملكة وافرة النفع في مصالح المدن وبها تدين العامة.
And it is not for a speaker to say that assent is more general than specific assent, so if a learner is convinced in principles in any way, he has benefited absolute assent even if he did not benefit specific assent. For we say: if the specific person were raised with such a description, an assent of the kind of general assent, it would be incumbent upon us to say that this address benefits him an assent even if it is not specific assent. But the one who perceives specific assent is not of the nature that assent benefits him except in the specific manner or what resembles it, which does not bring to mind its opposite. As for the common person, he does not perceive that, but rather takes the matter as assenting to it when his soul inclines towards it, and he proceeds to remove the opposite from his mind even if its argument appears to him. So his soul's inclination towards it is concomitant with assent and a cause for it, even if it is not the very assent; otherwise there would be no assent, nor a strong opinion, but rather like opinion and the soul's inclination produces assent for the common person, since his consideration is only the outward appearance of the thing, whatever it may be. In summary, just as the demonstrative address is not unlikely that it is intended for demonstration, and likewise the rhetorical address, so too the dialectical address is not unlikely that its use is diverted from its proper direction to the direction of assent. Indeed, the Book to which falsehood cannot come from before it or behind it has spoken, saying: 'Invite to the way of your Lord with wisdom and good exhortation and argue with them in the best way' (Quran 16:125). That is, with demonstration – for those who can bear it; 'and good exhortation' – that is, rhetoric – for those who stop short of that; 'and argue with them in the best way' – that is, the commendable widely-accepted opinions. So He gave precedence to demonstration and rhetoric because they are directed towards benefit, and dialectic is directed towards discussion. Rhetoric is a faculty abundant in benefit for the welfare of cities, and by it the common people adopt religion.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage is a rebuttal of an objection regarding the nature of assent (tasdiq) and a justification of the three types of address. The author first counters a claim that absolute assent suffices, explaining that a specialist requires specific assent, while a common person assents due to inclination. Then, he relates this to the three modes of address: demonstrative (burhani), rhetorical (khatabi), and dialectical (jadali), supporting his view with Quran 16:125. He interprets 'wisdom' as demonstration, 'good exhortation' as rhetoric, and 'dispute in the best way' as dialectic using commendable premises. He notes that demonstration and rhetoric are for benefit, while dialectic is for discussion. Rhetoric is especially useful for organizing cities and for the common people's adherence to religion.

Key Terms
تصديق
تصديق خاصي
تصديق عامي
ميل النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What produces assent for the common person according to the passage?
A) Demonstrative proof
B) Inclination of the soul
C) Specific proof
D) Dialectical argument

Key Takeaway
The effectiveness of an argument depends on the audience's epistemic level; the same discourse can produce different types of assent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a scholar and a layperson both hearing a proof for Allah's existence. Explain why the scholar requires demonstrative premises while the layperson may be convinced by rhetorical persuasion. Use the passage's concepts of specific and absolute assent.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
intermediate
10 min
Three Types of Address: Demonstration, Rhetoric, and Dialectic in the Quran
Author connects three logical arts to Quranic command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and differentiate demonstration (burhan), rhetoric (khataba), and dialectic (jadal) as three modes of address, and correctly apply the Quranic verse 16:125 to each.

Core Idea
Quran 16:125 codifies the three logical methods: demonstration for the wise, rhetoric for the masses, and dialectic for debate.

The author crowns his argument by referencing the Quran, which enjoins three methods of inviting to the path of Allah. This lesson unpacks the interpretation of these methods as the three classical logical arts: demonstration, rhetoric, and dialectic. You will learn how each serves a distinct purpose and audience.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Quranic verse
Find the verse in the passage: Quran 16:125, 'Invite to the way of your Lord with wisdom and good exhortation and argue with them in the best way.'
This verse is the proof text for the three methods.
2
Identify the three terms
The verse has three key terms: hikma (wisdom), maw'idha hasana (good exhortation), and jidal (disputation).
These are the three modes of address.
3
Match terms to logical arts
The author interprets: hikma = burhan (demonstration), maw'idha hasana = khataba (rhetoric), jidal = jadal (dialectic).
This interpretation is a standard one in Islamic logic.
4
Understand their purposes
Demonstration and rhetoric are directed towards benefit (fayda), while dialectic is directed towards discussion (mufawada).
Benefit here means producing knowledge or persuasion.
5
Note the special role of rhetoric
Rhetoric is a faculty beneficial for cities (mudun) and is the means by which common people adopt religion.
This highlights the practical importance of rhetoric in society.

وليس لقائل أن يقول إن التصديق أعم من التصديق الخاصي فيكون المتعلم إذا أقنع في المبادئ كيف كان فقد أفاد التصديق المطلق وإن لم يفد التصديق الخاصي. فإنَّا نقول إن الخاصي لو رفع له بمثل هذه الصفة تصديق من جنس التصديق العامي لكان يحق علينا أن نقول: إن هذه المخاطبة تفيده تصديقا وإن لم يكن تصديقًا خاصيًّا لكن الشاعر بالتصديق الخاصي ليس من شأنه أن ينفع له التصديق إلا على النحو الخاصي أو الشبيه به الذي لا يخطر ما يقابله بالبال . وأما العامي فلا يشعر بذلك بل يأخذ الأمر مصدقا به إذا مالت إليه نفسه، ويجري أن يمنط المقابل عن ذهنه وإن لاح له حواره فيكون ميل نفسه إليه مقارنا للتصديق، وعلة له وإن لم يكن نفس التصديق وإلا لا يكون هناك تصديق، ولا ظن مؤكد بل مثل ظن وميل النفس يوقع التصديق عند العامي؛ إذ نظره في ظاهر الشيء أي شيء كان. وبالجملة فكما أن المخاطبة البرهانية لا يبعد أن يراد بها العلية. وكذلك المخاطبة الخطابية فكذلك المخاطبة الجدلية لا يبعد أن يعدل باستعمالها عن جهتها إلى جهة التصديق. وقد نطق الكتاب الذي لا يأتيه الباطل من بين يديه ولا من خلفه فقال: ﴿ ادْعُ إِلَى سَبِيلِ رَبِّكَ بِالْحِكْمَةِ وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ وَجَادِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ ﴾ أي بالبرهان؛ وذلك ممن يحتمله وَالْمَوْعِظَةِ الْحَسَنَةِ أي الخطابة؛ وذلك ممن يقتصر عنه، وَجَادِلْهُم بِالَّتِي هِيَ أَحْسَنُ أي بالمشهورات المحمودة، فقدم البرهان والخطابة لما أنهما مصروفتان إلى الفائدة، والمجادلة مصروفة إلى المفاوضة ، والخطابة ملكة وافرة النفع في مصالح المدن وبها تدين العامة.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the term 'maw'idha hasana' (good exhortation) refers to:
A) Demonstration (burhan)
B) Rhetoric (khataba)

Key Takeaway
The three modes of address are not arbitrary; they are divinely ordained methods suited to different audiences and objectives.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Based on the passage, categorize the following activities: (a) a khutbah, (b) an academic theological debate, (c) a classroom lecture on 'aqida. Explain each using the terms burhan, khataba, jadal.
